3782 : BK 81.33 |BK 81.33: mwaṅ hana tâmuput salaga wāni pamaja nṛpati. ``Bud'' seems more acceptable than ``calyx'' (the ModJ slaga) in view of the comparisons involving waiting for the rain; also a young woman is compared to a salaga (Sum 65.1; 65.2). In combinations such as asana salaga, it is better to take salaga (``in bud'') rather than as a hybrid compound. The bal. com. render salaga with mĕnur, mlaṭi and pusuh (``closed bud''). Salaga niṅ mĕnur (Sum 164.3), however, shows that salaga and mĕnur are not the same.  salaga

4524 : BK 95.3 b|BK 95.3b: sumambut musuhnyeka pi ndan tujah den cacah cūrṇa saṅsāra denya n kĕna ndan pirul dan kumis len ikaṅ daitya mohâṅa#muk dan dinuk dan gutuk riṅ watu ndan pupuh den wunuh len tinalyan rinantaynya pan den dudut denya kady āmatĕk den waweṅ ambara; cf 96.8: maṅkin krodha Mahoda#râmurĕkakĕn hastinya pan den wĕlĕg. If we assume that den = (n)dan, this would explain forms such as den cacah alongside ndan pupuh (with loss of infix -um-), without resort to a passive (cf ndak warah kita). On analogy with passive forms using denya, dera etc, den may then have become a passive prefix.  de

4672 : BK 102.18 |BK 102.18: laṅgala minuṣṭi de nira masö / muṅgw i syandana śīghra yar putĕrakĕn ta sañjata nira. Uncertain: BrP 181.15: mamĕtwakĕn ikaṅ megha mehakĕn ikaṅ toya, mataṅ nyan megha ṅaranya; mataṅnyan abhra ṅaranya wih: abhranti yataś câpaḥ, ri denya n putĕrakĕn ikaṅ ākāśa (Skt BrP has: na bhraśyanti yataś câpas tad abhraṃ kawayo widuḥ).
